I had depression and during the course of it I was trying so hard to not lose my s/o because she's the only one that really made me happy, and I lost her anyway and it was the hardest thing in my life. He stops short of directly trying to excuse his actions through his sob story but the fact that they're in the same video is a conflict of interest enough for me.   What this video really is is a character rescue. Its fantastic production value, surface relatability and apparent apology will easily convince the average vapid Youtube user to forgive and forget. It's incredibly well made and targeted in that regard. This isn't a redemption arc in a show, it's not character development, it's a man admitting guilt and wanting to rebuild a ruined lifestyle.             Over the past year we have all been through rough patches, school, work, family, social life, etc. As much as my friends jokingly call me a "hipster" or "snob," coffee has been a point of control in my life. Something I can do with my hands and create a sufficient product with. I'm proud of the coffee I make and, at first, the precise measurements I went through to brew the perfect cup were holy ratios and sacred texts. When someone asks for a cup now, I find myself no longer worrying about whether or not I think it will be the absolute best coffee they have ever had. I find that the perfectionist in myself will allow me to make coffee for others without worry. I still don't know why. Maybe I've mastered it (although I know I haven't). My own tastes are satisfied with it. As each day passes, I've been allowing myself to mess up here and there, as it may lead to a different profile. I thought early on, this was just a passing hobby I'm getting way too into on account of my addictive personality. Instead, I find that I feel better after each cup brewed. It doesn't just feel like the latest hyperfixation, I can move at my own pace. I don't have to have top of the line equipment or watch 100 videos to find the perfect brew. I drink what I like and experiment with new things as they come to me.            To anyone reading this, I hope you're doing well. I hope you can find it within yourself to forgive but never forget. If we forget the experiences of the past we may never remember to forgive in the future. I'm no sage, nor will I pretend to be. I'm simply a man who will one day admit to his own guilt, and attempt to rebuild a ruined lifestyle he once knew. It may be something as small as skipping out on my gym day, or not finishing coursework on time. I may also royally screw myself by cutting off ties with a family member, or wishing upon someone's downfall only for my wish to come true. Whatever it may be, we will all constantly be rebuilding and learning from our mistakes. There is no reason to forget, but there will always be a reason to forgive.  If you are still here, thanks for reading. Please, have a wonderful day, and work towards forgiveness.

As it's been said so many times now, we all make mistakes. I'm glad to know you're learning from them. As somebody who has fucked up a lot in my life, I know all too well what hitting rock bottom feels, along with the importance of owning those mistakes and not pretending they didn't happen. Taking them and learning from them is what you need to grow and become something more. To transform into somebody *you* can be proud of.  I've been working on myself a lot more. For so long, I've been so selfless that it eventually became selfish. That statement may be hard to understand if you haven't lived it. It was so bad that even just the act of somebody loving me made me hate myself that much more. Happiness can never be external. Which is why games and music and other hobbies may not work now. We may think that's what makes us happy, but we have to look deeper. I always derive happiness myself by making other people happy, too. But that happiness isn't sustainable, because you just can't make everyone happy. So when I ruin relationships or I upset somebody, especially somebody I care about, I see it as a failure and I internalize that pain. I see it as I can't make *anyone* happy. I know that's not true, but in those times I can't think about it any other way. That's why working on yourself is so important.  For a lot of us, looking at ourselves is too hard, so we look at others and judge them or compare ourselves to them. It's easy to say we won't be like that or do that. But in all actuality, that's an impossible statement. I'm not you. I am me.  But then, who am I really? Well, I don't know. And honestly, that's the scariest thing. I'm 31 and have no idea who I am. My friends will tell you I'm a sweetheart with a heart of gold who enjoys doing things selflessly, even to a fault, if it helps another person. But the truth is... I just want to find happiness. My mental health has made that impossible for me, or feel impossible. My broken mind knows this which is why pleasing other people don't bring sustainable happiness.  Sorry for the essay. Just saying I know how it feels, Albert, to lose yourself. The journey we make to find ourselves is arduous, but needed. I don't exactly know what happened, either, but I truly hope you find that inner peace and one day that both of us can find a way to look in a mirror and be proud of who we see. Good luck, man. And good luck to everybody else who finds themselves here at rock bottom.
